بالتواتر من المعجزات وغيرها ، يقول أحد هؤلاء ـ بناء على هذا الفرق ـ هذا ما لم يتواتر عندي فلا تقوم به الحجة على أو ليس ذلك بشرط . ومن هذا الباب إنكار كثير من أهل البدع والكلام والفلسفة لما يعلمه أهل الحديث من الآثار النبوية ، فان هؤلاء يقولون إنها غير معلومة لنا . كما يقول من يقول من الكفار : إن معجزات الأنبياء غير معلومة له . وهذا لكونهم لم يعلموا السبب الموجب للفهم بذلك . والحجة قائمة عليهم ، تواتر عندهم أم لا »(۲) . نستخلص من هذه المناقشة العميقة لفكرة إنكار المنطق الأرسططاليسي ليقينية القضايا المتواترة مدى صحة النقد الإسلامي العام للمنطق الأرسططاليسي . فقد نقد المسلمون ، وتابعهم ابن تيمية ـ منطق أرسطو لما ينتجه تطبيقه على المسائل الدينية من متناقضات وإنكار . وهؤلاء المناطقة يرون أن القضايا المعلومة بالتواتر أو المتواترة ، يختص بها من علمها ، فما يتواتر عند شخص خاص به وليس خاصاً بغيره وعلى هذا فينهدم كثير من آثار الدين المتواترة ولعل هذا كان أكبر ما رنا إليه عبد الله بن المقفع وابنه محمد بن عبد الله حين قدما أول ترجمة للمنطق ، وهو إثبات يقينية المنطق بقضاياه العقلية والحسية ، وإنكار تواتر الدين ، الذي يستند على السماع فقط ولعل هذا أيضاً ـ ما دعا إلى إنشاء علم من أعظم العلوم الإسلامية ـ وهو علم مصطلح الحديث ، وفيه محاولة حاسمة لتحقيق الدراية والرواية ووضع أصول الجرح والتعديل ، للتوصل توصلاً حاسماً إلى صحة الأحاديث . وقد سبق المسلمون ـ كما سنوضح هذا ـ علماء مناهج البحث التاريخية في وضع هذا العلم . فكان علم مصطلح الحديث إذن رداً حاسماً على المنطق الأرسططاليسي . ويتبين لنا أيضاً من هذا العرض الجميل لابن تيمية ، صحة صرخة الفقهاء ـ حين نادوا ـ من تمنطق تزندق . كانت صرختهم من قلب الإسلام العظيم ، دفاعاً عن « التواتر » تواتر الكتاب والسنة بما فيهما من حقائق وأفكار ومذاهب .
And not due to the ignorance of others. So the physician and the philosopher among those who denied the mutawatirat have no intellectual proof negating these mutawatirat. The utmost they have is that in their discipline there is nothing that indicates the existence of mutawatirat. And this only yields absence of knowledge, not knowledge of absence, and the leading physicians and philosophers like Hippocrates and others have admitted this. The reason for which Ibn Taymiyya defends the certainty of mutawatirat and that it is not exclusive to those who know it, but he also argues with it against the opponent, is to rescue the certainty of hadith and its acceptance as a source of thought and legislation. Rather, Ibn Taymiyya defends prophethood and the tawatur of its books and miracles. Ibn Taymiyya says: Denial of mutawatirat are foundations of atheism and disbelief, for what is transmitted from the prophets via tawatur of miracles and other things, one of these people says—based on this distinction—'This has not reached me via tawatur, so the proof is not established for me'—or is that not a condition? And from this category is the denial of many of the people of innovation, speculative theology, and philosophy of what the people of hadith know of prophetic traditions, for these say they are not known to us. Just as some of the disbelievers say: The miracles of the prophets are not known to him. And this is because they do not know the cause necessitating understanding of that. And the proof stands against them, whether it is mutawatir for them or not. We extract from this deep discussion of the idea of the denial of Aristotelian logic of the certainty of mutawatirat issues the extent of the validity of the general Islamic critique of Aristotelian logic. For the Muslims, followed by Ibn Taymiyya, criticized Aristotle's logic for what its application to religious matters produces of contradictions and denial. These logicians hold that propositions known by tawatur or mutawatirat are exclusive to those who know them, so what is mutawatir for a person is special to him and not for others, and upon this many of the mutawatir traces of religion are destroyed. Perhaps this was the greatest aim of Abdullah ibn al-Muqaffa' and his son Muhammad ibn Abdullah when they first presented a translation of logic: to establish the certainty of logic with its intellectual and sensory propositions, and to deny the tawatur of religion, which relies on hearing only. And perhaps this also called for the establishment of a science among the greatest Islamic sciences—the science of mustalah al-hadith, in which there is a decisive attempt to achieve knowledge (diraya) and transmission (riwaya) and to lay down the principles of jarh and ta'dil, to decisively attain the authenticity of hadith. And the Muslims preceded—as we will clarify this—the scholars of historical research methodology in establishing this science. Thus, the science of mustalah al-hadith was a decisive response to Aristotelian logic. And from this beautiful exposition of Ibn Taymiyya, we also see the validity of the cry of the jurists—when they proclaimed: 'Whoever engages in logic has become a heretic.' Their cry was from the heart of great Islam, defending 'tawatur'—the tawatur of the Book and the Sunnah with their realities, ideas, and schools.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage presents Ibn Taymiyya's critical argument regarding the certainty of mutawatirat (recurrent reports) and uses it to critique Aristotelian logic. The author begins by noting that the denial of mutawatirat by physicians and philosophers is based on a lack of evidence within their disciplines, which only indicates absence of knowledge, not knowledge of absence. Leading figures like Hippocrates have admitted this. Ibn Taymiyya then defends the certainty of mutawatirat, arguing that it is not exclusive to those who have directly witnessed the reports; rather, it is universally binding. He links this defense to safeguarding prophethood and the transmitted books and miracles. Quoting Ibn Taymiyya, the author shows that denying mutawatirat is a foundation of atheism because it undermines the transmitted miracles of prophets. Some people claim that what is not mutawatir for them personally does not constitute proof, but this is not a valid condition. This denial is akin to the rejection of prophetic miracles by disbelievers, stemming from ignorance of the cause that necessitates understanding. The proof remains against them regardless of whether it is mutawatir for them. The author then concludes that this deep discussion demonstrates the validity of the general Islamic critique of Aristotelian logic. Muslims, including Ibn Taymiyya, criticized Aristotle's logic because its application to religious issues leads to contradictions and denial. The logicians' view that mutawatirat are exclusive to those who know them would destroy many established religious reports. This, the author suggests, was the hidden aim of early translators of logic like Ibn al-Muqaffa': to prioritize logical certainty over transmitted religious knowledge. In response, Muslims developed the science of mustalah al-hadith, which provides rigorous criteria for verifying reports, thus refuting the Aristotelian stance. The passage ends by affirming the jurists' warning that 'whoever engages in logic has become a heretic' as a defense of the tawatur of the Quran and Sunnah.

Key Terms
متواترات (mutawātirāt): Reports transmitted by a multitude of narrators at each level, which yield certain knowledge according to Islamic epistemology. [Note: In logic and theology, mutawātirāt are considered certain premises; in hadith sciences, they are the highest category of authenticity.]
تواتر (tawātur): The continuous transmission of a report by a large, independent group that precludes collusion, resulting in certainty. [Note: The concept is stable across usul al-fiqh, hadith, and mantiq, but its epistemological role is emphasized more in critiques of Aristotelianism.]
عدم العلم لا العلم بالعدم (ʿadam al-ʿilm lā al-ʿilm bi-l-ʿadam): The logical distinction between absence of knowledge (lack of evidence) and knowledge of absence (proof of non-existence). Used to refute the claim that unproven mutawatirat are false. [Note: This is a standard logical principle; Ibn Taymiyya uses it polemically.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) They are correct if the report does not align with logical premises.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Aristotelian logic on mutawatirat reveals that rejecting transmitted knowledge due to personal ignorance is a logical fallacy, and this critique spurred the rigorous science of hadith verification.

Ibn Taymiyya's Linguistic Critique of Greek Logic
Author presents Ibn Taymiyya's critique that Muslims need Arabic, not Greek logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's linguistic argument against Greek logic and identify its historical precedents.

Core Idea
Greek logic is language-bound; Muslims need Arabic, not Aristotelian forms.

Ibn Taymiyya argues that Greek logic is not a universal tool but is tied to the Greek language. He insists that Muslims must prioritize learning Arabic, which is essential for understanding the Quran and Sunnah. This lesson unpacks his critique and traces its roots to earlier scholars like al-Sirafi and al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being critiqued
Find the assertion that Greek logic is necessary or a communal obligation for Muslims. Ibn Taymiyya attributes this to Matta ibn Yunus, al-Ghazali, and some usulis.
Look for phrases like 'فرض على الكفاية' (communal obligation) and 'شرط للاجتهاد' (condition for ijtihad).
2
Extract Ibn Taymiyya's main objection
He argues that Greek logic is connected to the Greek language and its terminology, whereas meanings are intellectual and do not need such special terminology. Thus, learning Arabic is the true need.
Key phrase: 'فمنطق اليونان متصل بلغتهم' (logic of the Greeks is connected to their language).
3
Trace the critique's lineage
Ibn Taymiyya cites al-Sirafi, who first articulated the argument, and then al-Shafi'i via al-Suyuti. Al-Shafi'i linked the abandonment of Arabic to theological innovations like the claim of the Quran's creation.
Notice the reference to al-Ma'mun's era and the 'قَوْل بِخَلْق الْقُرْآن' (saying of the creation of the Quran).
4
Assess the critique's internal validity
Consider whether the critique is logically sound: does the language-dependence of Greek terminology invalidate its universal applicability? Ibn Taymiyya offers an alternative: the Quran and Sunnah follow Arab conventions, not Greek ones.
The passage concludes this critique is 'largely correct' (صحيحة إلى حد كبير).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فليس العقلاء إذن في حاجة إليه كما يدعي متى بن يونس ، وإنما في حاجة إلى تعلم العربية كما يذكر السيرافي « لأن المعاني عقلية لا تحتاج إلى اصطلاح خاص »(۱) بخلاف اللغة اليونانية التي تحتاج إلى اصطلاح خاص في معرفة ما يجب معرفته من المعاني . فمنطق اليونان متصل بلغتهم ، بل هو يقوم على عبقرية تلك اللغة ، فمن الحمق إذن أن يستخدمه المسلمون ، أو أنه لا يوثق بعلم من لا يعلم المنطق ( ويشير ابن تيمية هنا إلى الغزالي ) أو أن تعلمه فرض على الكفاية ، وأنه من شروط الإجتهاد ـ كما يدعي بعض الأصوليين إن تعلم العربية التي لا يمكن فهم القرآن والحديث بدونها وهو الذي ينبغي أن يعتبر فرضاً على الكفاية . وهذا النقد الذي يعتبر أقدم نقد وجهه علماء الإسلام للمنطق الأرسططاليسي لا نجده لدى أبي سعيد السيرافي فحسب ، بل قال به الشافعي أيضاً في نص ينقله إلينا السيوطي وهو « ما جهل الناس واختلفوا إلا لتركهم لسان العرب وميلهم إلى لسان أرسططاليس » ويعلق السيوطي على هذا بقوله ، وأشار الشافعي بذلك إلى ما حدث في زمن المأمون من القول بخلق القرآن ونفي الرؤية وغير ذلك من البدع . وأن سببها الجهل بالعربية والبلاغة الموضوعة فيها من المعاني والبيان والبديع ، الجامع لجميع ذلك قوله لسان العرب الجاري عليه نصوص القرآن والسنة وتخريج ما ورد فيها على لسان يونان ومنطق أرسططاليس الذي هو في حيز ، ولسان العرب في حيز . ولم ينزل القرآن ولا أتت السنة إلا على مصطلح العرب ومذاهبهم في المحاورة والتخاطب والاحتجاج والإستدلال لا على مصطلح يونان . ولكل قوم لغة واصطلاح (۲) فهذا النقد إذن وجد قبل إبن تيمية وقبل السيرافي . ويمثل وجهة نظر صحيحة إلى حد كبير .
Therefore, the intelligent have no need of it as Matta ibn Yunus claims; rather, they need to learn Arabic as al-Sirafi mentions: 'Because meanings are intellectual and do not need a special terminology,' unlike the Greek language which needs a special terminology to know what must be known of meanings. So the logic of the Greeks is connected to their language, indeed it is based on the genius of that language. So it is foolishness for Muslims to use it, or that one does not trust the knowledge of one who does not know logic (Ibn Taymiyya here refers to al-Ghazali), or that learning it is a communal obligation, and that it is a condition for ijtihad—as some usulis claim—while learning Arabic, without which understanding the Quran and Hadith is impossible, is what should be considered a communal obligation. This critique, which is the oldest critique leveled by Muslim scholars against Aristotelian logic, is not only found with Abu Sa'id al-Sirafi, but al-Shafi'i also said it in a text transmitted to us by al-Suyuti: 'People only became ignorant and disagreed because of their abandonment of the language of the Arabs and their inclination to the language of Aristotle.' And al-Suyuti comments on this saying: Al-Shafi'i indicated thereby what happened in the time of al-Ma'mun of saying the creation of the Quran, denial of the vision [of Allah], and other innovations. And their cause was ignorance of Arabic and the eloquence placed in it of meanings, clarity, and rhetoric, the sum of all that is his saying: the language of the Arabs upon which the texts of the Quran and Sunnah flow, and the extraction of what occurs in them upon the tongue of the Greeks and the logic of Aristotle, which is in one domain, and the language of the Arabs in another. The Quran was not revealed nor the Sunnah came except upon the convention of the Arabs and their ways in dialogue, address, argumentation, and reasoning, not upon the convention of the Greeks. Every people has a language and convention. So this critique, then, existed before Ibn Taymiyya and before al-Sirafi, and it represents a largely correct viewpoint.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage presents Ibn Taymiyya's linguistic critique of the need for Aristotelian logic. It begins by stating that intelligent people do not need such logic, as claimed by Matta ibn Yunus, but rather need Arabic. The author cites al-Sirafi's argument that meanings are intellectual and do not require a special terminology, unlike Greek which does. Thus Greek logic is tied to its language and is foolish to adopt for Muslims. The text also mentions that al-Ghazali required logic for trust in knowledge, and some usulis consider it a communal obligation, but the author argues that learning Arabic is the true communal obligation because it is necessary for understanding Quran and Sunnah. Then it traces the critique back to al-Shafi'i via al-Suyuti, who linked the abandonment of Arabic to the rise of theological innovations like the claim of the Quran's creation. The passage concludes that this critique predates both Ibn Taymiyya and al-Sirafi and is largely correct.

العربية
اصطلاح خاص

Key Takeaway
Greek logic is not a universal necessity for Muslims; mastering Arabic, the language of revelation, is the true communal obligation.

Mental Conceivability Does Not Prove External Existence
Ibn Taymiyya critiques mental possibility as a proof for external existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute the claim that mental conceivability proves external existence using Ibn Taymiyya's nominalist objection.

Core Idea
Conceivability in the mind does not guarantee reality outside.

Ibn Taymiyya targets a core logical move: using mental conception to prove external existence. He argues that we can conceive of things that have no external reality, such as the absolute universal man or the conjunction of contradictories. Let's unpack his critique step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophers' inference
Philosophers like Ibn Sina and al-Razi argue: we conceive of the absolute universal man in the mind, therefore it must have some external existence. This inference is based on the idea that mental possibility reflects external reality.
2
Ibn Taymiyya's counterexample: absolute universal man
Ibn Taymiyya points out that we can conceive of 'al-insan al-kulli al-mutlaq' (the absolute universal man) in the mind, yet no such universal exists externally—only particular individuals. This shows the inference is false.
3
Strengthen the objection: impossible things are conceivable
The mind can also conceive of impossible things like 'ijtima' al-naqidayn' (conjunction of contradictories), which can never occur externally. Thus, mental conceivability is not a reliable test for existence.
4
Formulate the critique as a modus tollens
If conceivability entailed existence, then impossible things would exist. They do not exist. Therefore conceivability does not entail existence. This refutes the philosophers' inference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينقد ابن تيمية أيضاً ابن سينا والرازي وغيرهما في اثبات « الإمكان الخارجي بمجرد تصوره في الذهن » فيرى أنهم حين أرادوا إثبات موجود معقول غير محسوس في الخارج . استدلوا على ذلك بتصور « الإنسان الكلي المطلق المتناول للأفراد الموجودة في الخارج » ويرى ابن تيمية أننا نستطيع أن نتصور في الذهن هذا الإنسان الكلي المطلق . ولكن الكلي المطلق لا يوجد في الخارج أبداً ، وليس كل ما يتصوره الذهن يوجد في الخارج . إن الذهن يتصور اجتماع النقيضين والضدين ، وهو ما لم يحدث أبداً . وللعقل تقاسيمه عن الوجوب والإمكان والإمتناع ولكن لا يتحقق كل ما في الذهن في الخارج إن ابن تيمية هنا إسمي بحت ، يغلو في الإسمية أشد الغلو . ويرى ابن تيمية أن المناطقة يخرجون بهذه الطرق الفاسدة الناس عما فطروا عليه من المعارف اليقينية والبراهين العقلية والأخبار النقلية السمعية . . . وبينوا لله وجوداً يستلزم الجمع بين النقيضين . ويحاول بهذا أن يثبت عقائده الكلامية من إثبات الصفات ووجود الله في جهة . فينكر ما يذهب إليه النفاة ـ من المتفلسفة والمعتزلة ـ من أن الله لا يباين المخلوقات ولا يجانبها ولا يشار إليه . ويقرر أن المنطق انتهى بهم إلى القضايا السلبية التي يصفون بها الله بما يسلبه عن صفات الكمال ، بل يجعلونه مشاركاً للممتنعات والمعدومات ، وتستلزم كون الموصوف بها معدوماً بل ممتنعاً . وأن هؤلاء سلموا بهذه الأصول وأفسدوا بها العلم عقلياً كان أو سمعياً . بينما مبنى العقل على صحة الفطرة وسلامتها . ومبنى السمع على تصديق الأنبياء ولم يأت الأنبياء بالخبر فقط . بل أتوا بالأدلة العقلية التي بها يعلم المطالب الإلهية التي يمكن علمهم بها بالنظر والاستدلال . أما الفلاسفة فقد انتهوا خلال منطقهم إلى « الوجود المطلق الكلي » أو المشروط بسلب جميع الأمور الوجودية . وقد تنبه ابن تيمية إلى أن الموجود المطلق الكلي في سلسلة الموجودات وهو الجنس الأعلى أقل الأجناس مفهوماً أو أقلها خصوبة ، فكرة مجردة لاحظ لها
Ibn Taymiyya also criticizes Ibn Sina, al-Razi, and others regarding the proof of 'external possibility by mere mental conception of it'. He sees that when they wanted to prove an intelligible, non-sensible existent in the external world, they inferred that by the conception of 'the absolute universal man encompassing the individuals existing externally'. Ibn Taymiyya holds that we can conceive in the mind this absolute universal man, but the absolute universal never exists externally, and not everything the mind conceives exists externally. The mind conceives the conjunction of contradictories and opposites, which has never occurred. The mind has its divisions regarding necessity, possibility, and impossibility, but not everything in the mind is actualized externally. Here Ibn Taymiyya is a pure nominalist, exaggerating in nominalism to the extreme. Ibn Taymiyya holds that the logicians, through these corrupt methods, take people away from what they are naturally disposed to (fitrah) of certain knowledge, rational proofs, and transmitted scriptural reports. They depicted for God an existence that entails the conjunction of contradictories. By this he attempts to prove his theological doctrines of affirming attributes and God's existence in a direction. He denies what the deniers – among the philosophers and Mu'tazila – hold, that God is not separate from creation, not opposite to it, and not pointed to. He asserts that logic has led them to negative propositions by which they describe God with what negates perfect attributes, rather making Him participate in impossible things and non-existents, and entail that the described is non-existent, even impossible. These people accepted these principles and corrupted thereby knowledge, whether rational or transmitted. While the basis of reason is the soundness and integrity of fitrah, and the basis of transmission is the belief in prophets. The prophets did not bring only reports; they brought rational proofs by which divine objectives are known, which they can know through reflection and inference. As for the philosophers, through their logic they arrived at 'the absolute universal existence' or existence conditioned by negating all existential matters. Ibn Taymiyya recognized that the absolute universal existent in the chain of existents, which is the highest genus, is the least in meaning or least in fecundity, a mere abstract idea with no share [in external reality].
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage continues Ibn Taymiyya's critical assessment of logicians, specifically targeting Ibn Sina, al-Razi, and others who attempt to prove external existence (like the existence of a non-sensible entity) by mere mental conception. Ibn Taymiyya uses the example of the absolute universal man (al-insan al-kulli al-mutlaq): we can conceive it, but it does not exist externally. He points out that the mind can conceive impossible things like the conjunction of contradictories, so mental conceivability does not guarantee external existence. The author (of Manahij Bahth) comments that Ibn Taymiyya here is a pure nominalist (ismi), exaggerating in nominalism. Ibn Taymiyya then broadens his critique: logicians, through these corrupt methods, lead people away from the certain knowledge inherent in fitrah (natural disposition), rational proofs, and revealed reports. He accuses them of depicting God in a way that entails contradictory attributes. He then contrasts his own theological position (affirming God's attributes and direction) with the philosophers and Mu'tazila who negate direction and separation. He claims that logic has reduced God to negative propositions, stripping Him of perfect attributes and equating Him with impossible and non-existent things. Ibn Taymiyya asserts that the foundation of reason is sound fitrah, and the foundation of transmission is belief in prophets, who brought not only reports but also rational proofs. He concludes that philosophers, through their logic, end up with the absolute universal existence, which is the highest genus – an idea that is the least meaningful and has no share in external reality.

Key Terms
الإنسان الكلي المطلق
اجتماع النقيضين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What example does Ibn Taymiyya use to show that mental conceivability does not guarantee external existence?
A) The concept of a necessary being.
B) The absolute universal man.
C) The resurrection of the dead.
D) The conditional supposition of al-Amidi.

Key Takeaway
Mental conceivability is insufficient to prove external existence; the mind can conceive of impossible things.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a claim in contemporary discourse (e.g., 'we can conceive of a perfect being, therefore it exists') and refute it using Ibn Taymiyya's method.
?
Find a hadith or Qur'anic verse that emphasizes reliance on fitrah over mere speculation, and explain how it supports Ibn Taymiyya's position.

Logicians Corrupt Fitrah and Distort Theology
Ibn Taymiyya accuses logicians of corrupting fitrah and distorting theology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how Ibn Taymiyya connects logical methods to theological errors and argue for the primacy of fitrah in epistemology.

Core Idea
Corrupt logic leads to corrupt theology.

Ibn Taymiyya broadens his attack: the logicians' methods lead people astray from the innate knowledge of fitrah and produce absurd descriptions of God, such as negative attributes that imply non-existence. Let's see how he builds this case.

Guided Path
1
Identify Ibn Taymiyya's claim about fitrah
He states that logicians, through corrupt methods, take people away from what they are naturally disposed to (fitrah) of certain knowledge, rational proofs, and transmitted reports.
Fitrah is the innate human disposition to know truth.
2
Specific theological error: God's existence entails contradiction
Ibn Taymiyya accuses logicians of depicting an existence for God that entails the conjunction of contradictories (ijtima' al-naqidayn), which is impossible.
3
Contrast with the correct approach
The prophets brought both reports (akhbar) and rational proofs (adillah aqliyyah). Therefore, sound reason and revelation are in harmony and aligned with fitrah.
4
Identify his own theological position
Ibn Taymiyya affirms God's attributes and direction (jihah), opposing those who negate direction and separation (philosophers and Mu'tazila). He claims their logical methods reduce God to negative propositions that make Him like non-existent things.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of the Abstract Necessary Existent
Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the philosophers' wajib al-wujud as mental fiction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the philosophers' necessary existent and apply his criteria for distinguishing real existents from mental fictions.

Core Idea
A lowly fly is more real than the philosophers' abstract necessary existent.

Ibn Taymiyya launches a devastating critique of the philosophers' concept of necessary existence (wajib al-wujud), arguing that it is a mere mental construct. He contrasts it with even the lowliest creature, which has positive attributes and thus greater reality. This lesson will walk through his argument and its implications for Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target
Find in the passage the exact claim Ibn Taymiyya is attacking: the philosophers' notion of a necessary existent stripped of positive attributes or described only by negations.
The target is from Ibn Sina's school, which defines wajib al-wujud as pure existence with no positive quiddity.
2
Extract the objection
Ibn Taymiyya objects that such an entity cannot exist externally because every external existent must have positive attributes. He calls it impossible (mumtani' al-wujud).
3
Analyze the comparison
Notice how Ibn Taymiyya uses a 'lowly existent' (mawjud haqir) as a foil: it shares the name 'existence' but is distinguished by a positive quality, making it superior to the philosophers' abstraction.
The lowly existent could be any contingent being like an insect—contrasting with the supposed pinnacle of existence.
4
Assess the conclusion
Ibn Taymiyya concludes that the philosophers' necessary existent is only in the mind, like other impossible things. This is a key move in his broader critique of metaphysics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الواقع ، بينما الله قمة الموجودات عند المنطق الديني لابن تيمية وجود خصب ثبوتي لا عدمي ذو صفات ثبوتية . وسيتغالى ابن تيمية فيما بعد : ويرى أن في الله المعين كل شيء ، بل سيذهب مع الكرامية إلى حلول الحوادث في ذات الله ، وذلك لكي يخصب في فكرة الله الغنية . ويقول ابن تيمية « وأما واجب الوجود الذي يثبتونه فإما أن يجعلونه وجوداً مجرداً من كل قيد ثبوتي أو عدمي . وإما أن يقولوا : بل هو مقيد بالأمور السلبية دون الثبوتية كقول ابن سينا وأمثاله وهذا إنما يوجد في الذهن لا في الخارج . فإنه يمتنع ثبوت موجود خارجي لا يوصف بشيء من الأمور الثبوتية، أو لا من الثبوتية ولا السلبية ، بل أي موجود حقير فرضته ، كان خيراً من هذا الذي لا يوصف بشيء ثبوتي ، فإنه قد شارك ذلك الموجود الحقير في مسمى الوجود ولم يمتاز عنه إلا بوصف عدمي . وذلك الموجود الحقير ، امتاز عنه بأمر وجودي، والوجود خير من العدم » ويرى ابن تيمية أنه طبقاً لهذا يتميز هذا الموجود الحقير عن واجب الوجود أكبر تمييز . إنه يتصف على الأقل بصفات ثبوتية . فمن الواضح إذن أنه « إن ما يثبتونه ويجعلونه واجب الوجود هو ممتنع الوجود، هو مفروض في الذهن ، كما يفرض سائر الممتنعات » . ويضيق ابن تيمية بدعوى المتفلسفة أنهم يتكلمون في الأمور الكلية والعقليات المحضة ، وبتقعرهم اللفظي - ووضع اصطلاحات لا توصل إلى شيء « الحقيقة من حيث هي هي » وغيرها من تعبيرات . فإذا ما طولبوا بإثبات أمورهم الكلية وعقلياتهم البحتة في الوجود الخارجي ، لم يستطيعوا ، ويدعون أن ما يقولونه هو أمر مقدر في الأذهان لا حقيقة له في الأعيان ، ولا يستطيعون إيراد مثال ، والمثال جزئي .
In reality, while God is the pinnacle of existents in Ibn Taymiyya's religious logic, [He has] a fertile, positive existence, not privative, possessing positive attributes. Ibn Taymiyya will later exaggerate: he sees that in God everything is present, rather he goes with the Karramiyya to the inherence of temporal events in God's essence, in order to fertilize the idea of a rich God. Ibn Taymiyya says: 'As for the necessary existent they affirm, they either make it an existence stripped of every positive or privative condition, or they say: rather it is restricted to negative attributes without positive ones, as Ibn Sina and his like say. This only exists in the mind, not in external reality. For it is impossible to affirm an external existent that is not described by any positive thing, or neither positive nor negative. Rather, any lowly existent you suppose is better than this one that is not described by any positive thing, because it shares with that lowly existent the name of existence and is distinguished from it only by a privative description. That lowly existent is distinguished from it by a positive quality, and existence is better than non-existence.' Ibn Taymiyya holds that according to this, this lowly existent is most distinct from the necessary existent. It is at least characterized by positive attributes. So it is clear that 'what they affirm and make the necessary existent is an impossible existence, it is assumed in the mind, as all impossibilities are assumed.' And Ibn Taymiyya is distressed by the philosophers' claim that they speak about universals and pure intelligibles, and their verbal profundity – and their coining of terms that lead to nothing, like 'the truth in itself' and other expressions. For if they are asked to prove their universals and pure intelligibles in external existence, they cannot, and they claim that what they say is something estimated in minds, having no reality in external objects, and they cannot give an example, and the example is particular.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage presents Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the philosophers' concept of necessary existence (wajib al-wujud). The author begins by situating Ibn Taymiyya's theological position: God is the pinnacle of existents, possessing a rich positive existence with attributes. Ibn Taymiyya then attacks the philosophers' notion of necessary existence, which they define as either stripped of all descriptions (both positive and privative) or restricted to negative attributes alone, as Ibn Sina held. Ibn Taymiyya argues that such a concept can only exist in the mind, not in external reality, because any external existent must have some positive attribute. He uses a contrast with a lowly existent (like a flea or dung beetle) that, despite its lowliness, has positive attributes, making it superior to the philosophers' abstract necessary existent. The lowly existent shares the name 'existence' but is distinguished by a positive quality, while the philosophers' entity is distinguished only by a privation (lack of positive attributes). Since existence is better than non-existence, the lowly existent is actually more real. Ibn Taymiyya concludes that the philosophers' necessary existent is impossible in external reality, only a mental fiction like other impossibilities. He also criticizes their empty terminology (e.g., 'the truth in itself') and their inability to give examples of their universals, because examples are always particular. This critique is rooted in Ibn Taymiyya's nominalist and empiricist approach.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود
موجود حقير
صفات ثبوتية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, why is a lowly existent like a fly superior to the philosophers' necessary existent?
A) Because the fly is physically larger.
B) Because the fly has positive attributes, while the philosophers' necessary existent has only negative or no attributes.
C) Because the fly is eternal.
D) Because the philosophers' necessary existent is material.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's critique shows that for an existent to be real outside the mind, it must have positive attributes; otherwise, it is merely a mental fiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Contrast Ibn Taymiyya's required positive attributes for a real existent with the Ash'ari position that God's attributes are eternal and distinct from His essence. How would Ibn Taymiyya evaluate the Ash'ari God compared to the philosophers' necessary existent?
?
Apply Ibn Taymiyya's critique to the philosophers' concept of the 'active intellect' (al-'aql al-fa''al). Does it have positive attributes? Is it considered an external existent? What would Ibn Taymiyya say?

The Theological Incompatibility of Greek Logic
Author summarizes Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Greek logic and its incompatibility with Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Ibn Taymiyya's claim that Greek logic is based on Aristotelian metaphysics and therefore incompatible with Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Greek logic is not neutral; it carries Greek theology that conflicts with Islam.

Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Greek logic is radical: he argues that logic is not a universal tool but is embedded in a particular worldview. In this lesson, we examine his fundamental charge that Aristotelian logic rests on metaphysical and theological premises that contradict Islamic teachings. Understanding this claim is essential for evaluating his broader methodological revolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central claim
Find where the passage states that Greek logic undermines Islamic civilization. Note the metaphor 'pickaxe' (معول). Then locate the sentence where Ibn Taymiyya says Aristotle's logic is based on his metaphysics and theology.
The passage uses strong language: 'the greatest pickaxe breaking the foundation of Islamic civilization'.
2
Extract the reason for incompatibility
The passage asserts that Aristotelian theology (إلهياته) contradicts Islamic theology (إلهيات المسلمين). This creates an impossibility of applying Aristotelian logic to Islamic divine sciences.
This is a radical claim: not just limited applicability, but outright incompatibility.
3
Assess the implication for Islamic sciences
Consider what it means if a method's foundational assumptions are at odds with Islamic beliefs. Does this mean all logical reasoning is rejected? Or only specific forms? The passage implies a call for an alternative methodology.
4
Connect to Ibn Taymiyya's alternative
Preview that Ibn Taymiyya proposes quantity and experimentation as foundations. This step sets up the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أدرك بعمق بالغ أن أعظم معول ينقض في أساس الحضارة الإسلامية، هو معول المنطق اليوناني. إنه سيقوضها باسم المنهج، وسينتج قضايا عامة في كل النطاقات تمزق الأحكام العامة للمسلمين، فتتبع قواعد هذا المنطق وقام بتطبيقها، فلم ينتج له سوى آراء بعيدة كل البعد عن ما هو إسلامي فأعلن أن منطق أرسطو إنما يستند على ميتافيزيقاه وإلهياته، وهذه الإلهيات مخالفة لإلهيات المسلمين، ومن هنا نشأت استحالة تطبيق مباحث المنطق الأرسططاليسي على مباحث المسلمين الإلهية. أما تطبيق مباحث المنطق الأرسططاليسي على مختلف العلوم، فقد رأى ابن تيمية ما في مباحث هذا المنطق من تكلف وتصنع، وتضييق طرق الذهن في نطاق معين هي « طرق صعبة طويلة، وعبارات متكلفة حائلة » وليس لها من نتيجة سوى إضاعة الوقت وإتعاب الأذهان. إن اتجاه الإسلام - كمنهج - أن يفي بالحاجات الإنسانية، والحاجة الإنسانية لا تستقر ولا تسكن، إنها في تغير مستمر فلا تتوقف فقط أمام « ماهيات جامدة » إن حقائق الأشياء الإنسانية والطبيعية في تغير مستمر، فنلجأ نحن فقط إلى تحديد أعراضها وخواصها أما أن يحاول اكتناه الماهية، فمطمع عسير. كما أن نتكلف قياساً يقتصر على مقدمتين، فان معناه أن نحصر أنفسنا في طرق ميكانيكية. كما أن من الخطأ أن نقتصر في الإستدلال العقلي على القياس والإستقراء والتمثيل، إننا نستطيع أن نصل إلى صور أكثر - إذا حللنا العمليات الفكرية، ولقد نادى ابن تيمية بفكرة « الكم » أساساً لكل عملية فكرية، ولم يؤمن بسلطان الكيف إلا نادراً، كما أنه لم يؤمن بالنظر البحت، بل نادى بالتجربة. إنه كان يتكلم باسم الروح الحضاري الإسلامي، ممجداً التجربة، معلناً أنها هي الطريق الوحيد للوصول إلى العلم سواء أكان يقينياً أو ظنياً. وسننتقل الآن الى مناقشة الجانب الإنشائي لنقد ابن تيمية لمباحث الإستدلال الارسططاليسي.
He realized deeply that the greatest pickaxe breaking the foundation of Islamic civilization is the pickaxe of Greek logic. It will undermine it in the name of methodology, and it will produce general issues in all domains that tear apart the general rulings of Muslims. So he followed the rules of this logic and applied them, but it produced only opinions far removed from what is Islamic. So he declared that Aristotle's logic is based on his metaphysics and theology, and this theology contradicts the theology of Muslims, hence the impossibility of applying the inquiries of Aristotelian logic to the divine inquiries of Muslims. As for applying the inquiries of Aristotelian logic to various sciences, Ibn Taymiyya saw in the inquiries of this logic artificiality and affectation, and a restriction of mental paths within a specific scope, which are 'difficult long paths, and pretentious elusive expressions' with no result other than wasting time and tiring minds. The direction of Islam - as a methodology - is to fulfill human needs, and human need does not settle or rest; it is in continuous change, so it does not stop only at 'static essences'. Indeed, the realities of human and natural things are in continuous change, so we only resort to determining their accidents and properties. As for attempting to comprehend the essence, it is a difficult aspiration. Also, that we burden ourselves with a syllogism limited to two premises means that we confine ourselves to mechanical methods. Also, it is wrong to limit rational inference to syllogism, induction, and analogy; we can reach more forms - if we analyze intellectual operations. Ibn Taymiyya advocated the idea of 'quantity' as a foundation for every intellectual process, and he rarely believed in the authority of quality, as he did not believe in pure speculation, but called for experimentation. He spoke in the name of the Islamic civilizational spirit, glorifying experimentation, declaring that it is the only way to reach knowledge, whether certain or probable. And we will now move to discuss the constructive side of Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the inquiries of Aristotelian inference.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage presents Ibn Taymiyya's fundamental critique of Greek logic as the author of Manahij Bahth summarizes it. The critique begins with the claim that Greek logic is the greatest tool undermining Islamic civilization because it operates under the guise of methodology but produces general rulings contrary to Islamic principles. Ibn Taymiyya asserts that Aristotle's logic is inseparable from Aristotle's metaphysics and theology, which contradict Islamic theology; therefore, applying Aristotelian logic to Islamic theological inquiries is impossible. When it comes to other sciences, Ibn Taymiyya finds Aristotelian logic artificial and restrictive, describing its methods as 'difficult long paths' and 'pretentious elusive expressions' that only waste time. Islamic methodology, by contrast, aims to fulfill dynamic human needs, which cannot be captured by static essences; we can only know accidents and properties, not essences. Furthermore, restricting reasoning to a two-premise syllogism is mechanical and limiting; we should not limit inference to syllogism, induction, and analogy but can reach more forms by analyzing intellectual operations. Ibn Taymiyya instead advocates for 'quantity' (al-kamm) as the basis of all intellectual processes, rejecting the authority of 'quality' and pure speculation in favor of experimentation (tajriba), which he considers the only path to certain or probable knowledge. The passage ends with a transition to the constructive aspect of Ibn Taymiyya's critique.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason Ibn Taymiyya considers Greek logic incompatible with Islam?
A) It uses Greek terminology that is difficult for Muslims to understand.
B) It relies on Aristotle's metaphysics and theology, which contradict Islamic theology.
C) It is too focused on experimentation, which is not valued in Islam.
D) It requires knowledge of mathematics, which is not an Islamic science.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya argues that Greek logic is not a neutral tool but is rooted in Greek theology, making it incompatible with Islamic theology and methodology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a contemporary argument in Islamic discourse that uses a method or framework originating from non-Islamic sources. Evaluate whether the method carries hidden metaphysical assumptions that might conflict with Islamic teachings, using Ibn Taymiyya's approach as a model.
?
Compare Ibn Taymiyya's claim that Aristotelian logic is based on Greek theology with the claim made by later scholars (e.g., al-Taftazani) that logic is a neutral tool. Which position do you find more convincing based on the passage?
